de la circoncision	On circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not necessarily a dislocation of continuity like other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our own will and properly for children, it must be done the best way, and in the easiest manner for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not mention the circumcision of their children, for they do not practice it in their laws, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have wanted the greatest part of masters and saints who performed circumcision between one day and three days, and at all times; they were buried with two sheets, and occasionally, the coffin was placed above and below the body.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or it recovers with copper, and the pain is doubled, and at the disfigurement which is hard to assure are not the tips of the member; and at the manicuring of the nail by chance slips away the iron, causing infection, and many times arise thus there is no need for further treatment as I have observed.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the manicuring done with force throughout all parts of the line I have found the benefit of experimentation, for the forces cut precisely both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez. li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	If the issue of inflammation is when the kernel inside escapes during incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your fingernail, so too does the head make an abscess; and cover equally, and if you cannot hold by your fingernail, then with tweezeboarers, and thereafter bandage.

And if they pass three days, and that which is from beneath the rod is swollen, let it be until the abscess has soothed; gently scrape it off; bandage as you move, and protect the area of the rod, for it will not do harm in any way.

Therefore heal the sudden wounds of powder that we have mentioned in treating powders, and if you bandage too much, and it goes beyond, it will not harm; heal as we have said until they are healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The retention of urine is due to obstruction by a stone, frozen blood, bowel, or similar things that we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine does not flow and you observe the retention caused by the stone located at the bladder neck or urethra base, then it is necessary for the patient to be bedridden with his knees bent; and let him lie on his back, stretching his belly towards the upper part of the back, and restrain the patient as much as possible; and then you must exert pressure on the bladder neck causing urine release from above, so that urine is flowed out; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, it is necessary to administer extraction with all the tools called "catheter", of which here is the form: made of finely hammered silver wire, like bird feathers; and its diameter should be one palm wide half, and very thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 The manner of relieving the issue with urination is to take a double thread and tie it at one end with a small piece of wool or cotton, then insert this into the catheter tube; remove excess wool up to the top of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and balm of aloes, have the sick person sit on a stool, and apply oily oil and olive oil to their bladder and penis. Then gently insert the catheter into the penis until it reaches near the base at the root, then extend the tube upwards towards the scrotum; next insert the syringe past this point up to the bladamoor, then sense when the patient feels a voiding sensation before reaching their empty urinary reservoir. If not done according to order because the conduit has been twisted, extend the thread little by little so that urine follows it and remove it once emptied; start again until the bladder is completely drained, then relieve the sick person of discomfort.
des maladies de la vessie	of bladder diseases
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are wounds or blood in the bladder, and decay has gathered there, and you see it needs to be cleansed with waters and medicines, so do all on the instrument called "clenched fist". Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed, and if it has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; the upper valve through which medicinal matter should be squeezed out well so that the shaft extends sensuously without addition, if possible to extract moisture, and insert as needed; and when you see your medicines in the bladder, place the head of a catheter into the moisture, and draw through the tube that is there; from the tube you will extract the moisture with a catheter, then firmly reset it back in; thus the moisture will enter, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the subtle form of the enema by which we cleanse the bladder: this is how.

de la piere	Of stone removal
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have discussed in the section the methods of stone removal and extraction along with medicines; we also described the difference between stones placed by rain, all signs, and where one must operate on sizeable stones; as well as within the bladder and penis; I will now clearly and briefly explain to you.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that stones placed within the bladwarthey occur more often in children and it is a sign of urine flowing from the bladder like water in its subtlety; and there are sand-like substances, and graininess in their penises, and they frequently pass them, then become lodged; and many suffer these stone movements; healing for children is relatively easy until they have reached four years of age, but it becomes very severe with adults and moderate for those between youth and old age; the treatment of larger stones is easier than that of smaller ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema in order to expel all filth from the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For sometimes it causes blockage of stones.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by hand and stand him up to move backwards, so that the stone descends towards the front of the bladastery, and sometimes comes out from below; then make the patient sit between your hands properly, with their hands behind their thighs so that the bladastery is completely inclined forward; then grasp and touch inside. If you feel the stone in its place, hurry to cut into it now.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not come out with the probe, moisten your left index finger with oil, if the patient is young or of middle age, and do so with your middle finger if they are mature; then press on its base, grasp the stone, and when you feel it at your finger, insert it to the neck of the bladastery; then apply pressure with your finger, and move it out as you saw.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and he commands him to extend the nails of his right hand upward, and to remove the skin from under the nails on his left hand in the part where one makes an incision; then he applies the spatula copiously, which forms it.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And they form between the one who is between the hips and the base, not in the middle but along the left side of the neck; and it is straight above the shoulder blade, and the hands are thus close or to the base, and the body has a hole so that it is wide at the front due to deficiency, and internally narrow, according to the amount of stone, not too large; perhaps pressing on the hand that is by the base or foundation, making them move easily without pain; and know that there may be part of the stone or corners and edges: they are easier to remove; and if a part rests on itself, similar to a glint, and round, from which it is easily removed.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 If there are angles and borders, make the hole larger; and if it does not come out, then it is necessary to use pincers similar to a file on its head, in order to extract the stone without slipping; or strike with a delicate instrument curved at the top; and if you cannot manage this way, enlarge slightly the exit opening, and if it becomes calcified, strain with vitriol; and if there are more than one stones, first remove the largest near the bladder neck, then towards the front, then the long one, and afterwards any smaller ones that remain.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, then one must suck it, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 For there are two things that happen to the patient: either they die or urine returns through a gap where the flesh cannot heal; however, always strive with traction and debridement using forceps until you have cleaned the wound in pieces; after completing your work, apply the wound with incense, aloe, and dragon's blood, along with pressure, and place a cloth soaked in oil and vinegar or oil, rose water, and cold water to cool the abscess. Then dress the patient on their bed, without loosening the bandage until the fourth day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you reset it, it is raised well with oil and water, then treated with the final diafinitus ointment and basilisk ointment until healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 When an abscess comes into the wound and causes corrosions and clotting of blood in the bladder, leading to retention of urine which is known by its lack of bubbling with urine: then place your finger in the wound, extract that blood, for if it remains, it will cause inflammation in the bladastereum and pelvis; then cleanse the wound of water and debris and hair, and aid him in all ways you know how until he is healthy; and it is necessary to tie both his thighs and apply remedies at its location.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 If the stone is small and it moves from the penis, and protrudes inside, and urine cannot pass; treat as I have described before, by dilating many times using this method of treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already found such a case.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take an iron rod according to this shape and make it with three sharpened edges in one section:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take a filament and wrap it around the shaft below the stone, so that it cannot return to the bladder; then insert the probe gently into the shaft until it reaches the stone; rotate the probe slowly in your hand against the stone from the other side; soon urine will come out, then press your hand where the remnant of the stone is lodged within the sheath.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.
