Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	 The fire cautery combines two things: it stops the bleeding of adjacent wounds and prevents the evacuation of moisture; then it treats dirty sloughs with oil or ground cloth, until the wound is thoroughly dried out, after which it heals the abscesses caused by strong ointments applied directly to the flesh. Then the treatments are completed once the medicines have had time to take effect.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it heals well and does not recur.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	the ch: :e cra�[S:
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	 If you find the slough and within it is loose canvas or flesh that needs to be cut open, do not attempt it without confidence and hope through proper management of one of these three methods: either cauterize as we have said, or excise until bare bone, or if possible treat and heal as previously; just don't go too deep so you don't seal off the foundation area, allowing for natural evacuation when ready. Then proceed to cure it as we have instructed; perhaps it will be beneficial without needing to remove that layer of skin near the base or with another instrument prepared elsewhere; then assess any additional wound debris and cleanse what has been excised; finally, examine how best to restore the wound and maintain the fistula further from the foundation: this would be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	 At no time are there fistulas according to this method: and it is when you push the tent into the fistula, and it is close to the foundation near the skin above, so take a pierced tent in the shape of this form.
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And he inserts a twisted thread of two lengths, and pushes the tentacle throughout the abscess until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	 If it is pierced near the foundation within, then remove the thread from that perforation and push your finger or foundation through it; and twist the head of the thread, and bring together both heads, holding them tightly against each other, and leave for one or two days; do not release at any time until the threads hold what is between them and pull apart; then treat the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the abscess is not healed through drainage, it should be cut in all possible ways if it does not penetrate too deeply.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not necessary to make a large incision at first, and then treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	 The shape of the spatulate splinter used to make a fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting on the other; however, not all should be torn as that which cannot or should not be torn.
des emorroydes	by.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 Dislodgements occur in two ways: either within the foundation, like resin grains which can be small or large, causing blood to flow and having one or several of them, affecting both the foundation and its chief; but those that are dislodged have little moisture, and from there emerge a bit of yellow water or some blood, retaining their body color. The treatment for those within the foundation is such: command the patient to sneeze so they can enter chambers until the foundations fall out, and filaments are visible; if hastened, grasp it with pincers at your fingernail, then cut its roots; and if the pincers cannot hold due to moisture, grasp them by thread or cloth piece from a camel skin. Then extract between your fingers, clip, and powder over hot powders that are ready for cautery; or cauterize as described in the chapter on cautery, since it heals other wounds until they become healthy; and if foundations cannot fall out, clisterize the patient with a sharp, rough clister to cleanse what is at the foundation, so that it can come out openly; when patients sneeze, and filaments are firm at the foundation, then treatment is easy. So grasp them by your fingernail or pincers, clip, then treat as we have said until they become healthy, avoiding incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is necessary to dress the wound as follows: take a twisted thread and put it on a needle, then pass the thread through from above and pierce the other side with the needle, turn the two loops of thread away from the needle, and make them wide; tighten the thread firmly, then moisten the thread, remove the needer, and do so for all others, leaving some excess blood to drain; then place a linen cloth smeared with rose oil or cerot on the base, put it in place, and command the patient to rest; then let it remain until they bleed, and when they have bled sufficiently, treat with ointment and other remedies until healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Firstly the foundation or groundwork
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times it frequently happens that there is blockage in the intestines and due to natural constraint, especially when illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is necessary to scrape off the skin at the top of a stud or your fingernail that does not allow moisture; then cleanse until it is dry as needed; and if it cannot dry, resume scraping more vigorously than before, until it is thoroughly dry, and be scarified; then cleanse until it is sufficiently dry.
dou fremit	The heat of fire cauterization causes slight tremors.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 A formication is a small faulty appearance around the body, and it spreads widely; and never does the blood turn blue, but the smell is like deathly shaking, and comes throughout the entire body, especially in the hands.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 And the treatment is to take a quill from a goose feather or a strong vulture feather, and place that quill on the shaking area until it turns purple throughout; then turn your hand all over with the quill as you cover completely around the shaking area, spreading it widely, and scrape the shaking down to its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see it, make a chain of iron or steel in this manner, and be subtle below and traverse above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not perceive with the eyes, but hold it in both hands and press it firmly; And if you see it, cauterize the tremor as if it were before or a fire cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	the uue et:
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	At no time is an enema made of silver or brass, or melted lead or molten metal; and at no time are these small and large suppositories prepared according to the substances they contain.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	However, those which are made in the treatment of children who are weak and sorrowful should be small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small and large enema is as follows, depending on whether the belly is tied up in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 and it has an opening or the stomach is tied up, as you see, and the chest is pierced inside; and have to one side two holes, and on the other side also. Apply the medicines of a bladder beast or parchment paper to the belly, and pierce all around through small holes, leaving space between each hole, then insert a strong thread made from twisted thread, surrounding it as in a goat's skin; and when the medicine is inside, tie it with a strong thread at one end of the instrument, then perform an enema; and this is the circular form.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 And the medicine should not be too hot or too cold, apply oil or goose egg butter to the enema tip, then pour it gently; then guide the instrument with both hands together until it is fully inserted, then extract the enema, and allow the patient to lie on their back as the medicine flows out, as much as possible; and if they sleep through the night entirely, this provides greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you administer the enema for a bowel disorder, and the medicine needs to be expelled quickly, repeat until he is healthy again.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if the hemorrhoid is at its foundation or abscess, then it should be treated with a subtle enema as for an infant; and that is the way to tighten the bowels during such a delicate enema.
des plaies	Of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	In the division of wound care, we have said previously; now let us discuss treatments for hands and medicines according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on how they are made, and by what causes or ways the wounds are made, and for what reasons they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 The things through which wounds are made include the cutting of stones and swords or spears, lances, bows, slings, or similar objects; or those made according to body parts, such as a wound that bleeds from the neck, head, groin, abdomen, liver, and similar limbs. And I will tell you about the treatment for each wound, starting with simple head wounds because memory serves in this chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 When a simple wound or head injury occurs and the bone is not broken, be cautious if it's from a stone throw or similar things, and the skin is fully torn with large wounds, and you suspect a heated abscess: immediately treat the head region if there is little blood flow from the wound, apply the remedy opposite to the affected area; and avoid replenishing the patient with wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it does not need to be treated with meat, and drink no wine or eat any meat, place it on the wound; if an abscess comes from there, apply a cotton ball soaked in oil only, or in vinegar-infused wine; and if no hot abscess is present, apply it where the wound is fresh with all its blood, and not moved by air or dust, I will tell you something later on that; and if it has been moved, apply some ointments until healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, with edges that cannot be joined by stitches, join them by suturing, as I will say for abdominal wounds, in sewing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound is exposed to bone, and sharp, and holds only slightly; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard-dry leather in its place, and instruct the patient to eat fatty meats like tested wheat, also as well cooked poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if you find or skin rot, and it does not adhere to the bone, cut off all rotten flesh, then wash thoroughly with wine vinegar; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein without a clot, and cannot be stopped by medicines, try tying the artery; and if that doesn't work, cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: apply this powder that dries just as salt causes things to move.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 The manner of the powder is as follows: take incense one part; blood of dragon two parts; lively chalk three parts, and grind finely, apply to wound, tightly bind, until it is well aired and joins all its blood; then wrap it up well, leaving no gaps unless it swells.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never perform this treatment solefly; when there is no incense or dragon's blood, but the physician has not healed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the wound has moved slightly, especially in this case, do not apply this powder but instead put on digested ointments or wheat flour made with water and honey until it heals; then continue with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if there is a fractured bone with the wound, and it is small, extract using fine tweezers; and I will tell you here about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	From a wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes from the neck and it is straightforward, without any difference between it and that of the head, but if the veins or the artery in the neck are damaged.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it is the nerves, with no other remedy but to leave the wound; do not place anything constricting on them, as this harms and draws back the nerves; and do not put anything cold on the wound because the nature of the nerves is cold, and their continuation comes from the brain, which is the highest body member. However, use medicinal spices soaked in gently warmed water with rose oil, heated likewise in gently warmed water, and other mineral substances prepared in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then bind it with bandages; then treat until healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 If the wounds are deep and swollen with pus, either puncture them or place it lower; if the arrowhead is removed, and blood flow occurs, drain it, remove any clots, and cauterization may be necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and conduits are guarded, which determines how tissue moves, so adjust according to its natural shape; then apply a bandage immediately, leave for several days, then treat with medicated ointments until healed; and if there has been pressure on the bone from the wound, seek it out; and if there are fragments of bone, remove them entirely or those that you cannot get, let the wound crust over, cleanse, and close the opening; and if the wound is fresh, apply powder to the area I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones and a fistula in the wound, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	ete toun:
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a wound from a lance or knife, and the injury is deep, look to see if there are swellings around the area where the patient feels pain: then know that the wound is lethal; but if it's not deep and the entire blood supply is fresh, do not apply powder immediately nor bind with a bandage as the blood may flow out further, causing harm to the body; instead use an attracting ointment, and reapply twice in one day. If you don't have ointment, put some old cotton into the wound to absorb moisture, and let the patient rest on their back for three or four days, or longer; then there won't be any spasms, nor tremors of body pain or limb dislocations. And when you see good healing signs, know that the wound is cured.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Treat with bandages and other treatments until healed; and if it cannot be healed or worked upon, then determine that there is a fistula; perform the treatment as should be done.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision and it's simple or located on the back, treat that which is in front; if it's large, with bandages; and if it's small, with powder, and if it's embedded in the bone, remove as much of the wound and foreign objects as possible; and if not, let the wound heal naturally, making the extractions easier; and for other wounds on different limbs, make judgments as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	During a rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The collapses of the abdomen are large and medium and small; from a great wound never emerges any intestine or nerves of the intestines, causing infiltration thereof; and suturing is more difficult, and never worse than a small wound, because when resetting the intestines they require more effort, unless they are reset gradually by heat; for the intestines swell almost immediately upon feeling cold, thus they return with greater force, and therefore a superficial wound moves easier, because one resettles the intestine to its place as do others. Also know that treatments of abdominal collapses come in four ways: common sutures occur on the abdomen's opening, and sutures from other body injuries and two specialized methods are also shared; nonetheboever these are more suited to the abdomen's opening, and I will describe each one individually.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 When the wound is small and there are no issues with the internal organs to be concerned about, and only minor things need to be reset as we have said: either because of the size of the wound or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: by moistening with an sponge or a piece of cloth briefly soaked in hot water, or by pouring boiling vinegar and salt and pepper over the wound until the swelling subsides; do not repeat this process too often, and ensure to dry it out to reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the swelling subside, moisten the intestines with warm or hot water as necessary because it allows passage for minimal matter; and if there is no entry, make a small incision using the instrument used to cauterize hemorrhoids; the first treatment is to dilate the opening, without any great need for cutting unless required: this is done by slicing inside the cavity and not towards it, then observing its shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 When the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have burst forth, if you can reset it according to its natural form in its proper place, if possible, because this allows movement.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is large and located below the belly, it is necessary to make the patient lie on their back, with legs raised higher than their head; if it's below the belly, raise the head and hips higher than the lower parts, and similarly arrange in such a way that the wounded part is elevated above the rest. In this manner, attend as I say for large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 For small wounds use the following method: have it bandaged with a pitiable cloth in your hands, then assemble the edges; this is the common way for sutures and that you take a needle or several depending on the width of the wound, leaving from the head of the wound I finger's length, and insert an eyelet or more with a good strong thread; puncture both sides of the skin with two eyes at the base, and as long as you do so, gather those two edges together until they are aligned in pairs. Then stretch a double thread around the needle from both ends, then bring the edges of the wound together again, leaving I finger's length apart, and insert another eyelet; tie the thread like your first stitch, without stopping as long as you need to secure all the stitches; use medium-sized eyes that are neither too small nor too large, because very small ones won't cut through well and very large ones can't enter properly. The second method of suturing with eyelets is more suitable for small wounds because it uses only one needle or two if needed, assemble the edges of the skin and fat together at a time using a strong thread; then put a bandage on the eyes to prevent them from sticking when rested, and leave as long as the wound is stitched.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I brought back the intestines as it had been XXIV hours since, and the wound was dressed until day fifteen, and I treated him, and he became well.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 And the master believed he would die, and it was a miracle; I did not treat him with ointment because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine; instead, twice daily, I placed old cotton over the wound and washed it with honey water until he became well.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 Or I will tell you two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and thread it through to the point where the skin is thickest; when it pierces straight ahead on the correct side or wherever you inserted the neede, pass it back out from another part inside until reaching that same place; and the understanding of this stitch is to sew as a tailor would with leather pieces, leaving one edge once pierced and then the other, continuing so until the entire suturing is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second method of suture, as Galien properly states, is similar to any other, which joins the two parts together naturally and applies one end of the silk thread to the other end in such a manner: pierce with a needle or fine silk near where it's needed, puncture only slightly at that location leaving both ends of the sinew; then turn the needle, and pierce from that part forward until reaching inside as close to those two ends of the sinew; then pierce each end of that part forward in two other pieces of fine silk that are on the opposite side; this is the manner of suture and it's most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galien says this word and others attest to it: one must sew the abdomen with two needles, each having thread; and push one needle from one side, and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew belts; and know that when the suture is amidst the abdomen, then this method of suturing is more difficult than others on the rest of the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgments of the wound are such as with other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound fully moved, thus straighten its intestines and stitches; then apply powdered charcoal, and if the artery has moved, put on any ointment present until the wound heals; and cut a slit, and be sure it is sealed, and lined with mirabilis herb, then treat the wound as others, until it becomes healthy again; and if you have no medicines, apply cotton swabs immediately when it starts to fester, move them twice daily until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 For in certain conditions the wounds are simple and require no other medicine besides; and if you doubt that the wound is causing community among the principal members, then lightly moisten with warm oil or rose oil, placing it around the joints and under the ankles; and if there is pain or swelling in the groin, which often occurs, perform a wine-blackened vinegar enema, especially if the swelling reaches the intestines; and probe internally, knowing that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine called "jeun" cannot heal when it is distressed, and this is because of the proliferation of veins within it, and due to the subtlety of the entire body, and its closeness to the nervous system.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 If the sinew springs from the wound, reset it as with the intestines while fresh; and if it becomes old or blackened, then you must remove the dark area to prevent blood flow due to veins and arteries; then address what is between the ligaments, and place two pendulous heads below the part above the wound until they ease the extraction as sinews heal, and the wound bows.
de la routure dou boueil	From the treatment of boils
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestines are inflamed and the wound is small, it can be restored in some cases because I saw a man was afflicted with an abdomen from a lance; the wound was on the right side of the stomach, became swollen, and turned into a fistula, resulting in evacuation and winds; I treated according to what I could do, and did not cease subtlety until it was healed, and the seeds were sown.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I saw it welded together, I doubted that the patient had pain in his belly; but there was no harm at all, just better conditions, eating and drinking; and some experienced observers said that if there is a small wound inside the intestine, it should be tied off thus: take large testes, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the fumes pass through the mouth, they stretch their mouth over two lips, so it pulls out; and then cover the head, and keep it that way until it cannot come apart, then put another fume after in the same manner as before, until the entire wound is closed; and cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 The head swells in the intestine and causes no harm to the patient; one can tie the intestine with a thin thread cut from an animal's intestine: take the end of this thread of intestine that is quite dry, then bind it with a fine linen thread twisted tightly, put the thread through the needle, and sew the intestine, ensuring proper stitching; this method of frantic stitching does not vary unless by trust and hope. And if the wound is large and wide, especially when located in one of the internal organs, there is no remedy or health without subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	From a fistula or where it may be found
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 When any wound or abscess ages, it is universally called 'fistula', especially when it swells and becomes protruding.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 A fistula is caused by the incorrect location of blood vessels and skin, where there is no pain felt, and it swells like a bird's feather; at times clearly protruding, and at other times thickened; sometimes hard, and at other times soft; among all wounds not properly treated, and if they are untreated, this occurs for one of the nine reasons: namely, due to lack of blood or tissue; or because it is malignant; or there is a hardening inside that does not allow healing on its surface; or excessive swelling; or the wound area is inflamed, and the material is of poor quality; or the medicine used for treatment is not good; or due to decay being a form of pestilence; or because of the late digestion in that region, resulting in slow healing naturally; or if there are foreign bodies or bone. I have already demonstrated all these causes, their signs, and medical treatments in the section on wounds.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary for me to teach you about the treatment of an abscess, which is done by handiwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Leaking occurs in all parts of the body; for there are leaks that come from large veins and arteries, and nerves, or to the liver, or intestines, or bladder, or to certain ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of hands or feet; and if it comes near the principal part of a limb, and other areas.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 Leaks of this nature are difficult to heal, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any leak that does not come close to where I have mentioned, and you trust in its cure, and see it confirmed, then take a tent from wax or iron if the fistula is straight, use it; and if the fletee is twisted, search with a finer tent made of lead, for lead can bend around the tortuosity; and if the fistule has many openings and you cannot well trace them by tents, clysterize through one of the orifices, as moisture will flow from one opening to another, and cleanse it. Then gently cope with your power, asking the patient about pain felt at the pressure of your hand and where it is felt; and when you know truly where it is, and whether it's away from a joint, nerve, artery or vein, or in any of the areas I have mentioned, follow my instructions to cure accordingly, removing foul matter and hardened pus within. Then continue the treatment until healed, and if the fistulee is deeply straight, cope with it completely as much as you can see; then apply moist bandages soaked in medicinal water, filling them up to the top of the fistule, until the medicine corrodes the excess material at its bottom. Then apply balms mixed with curative herbs until they are healed; and if it is not healed by this, cauterize as I have said before, and if bone has been affected by the fistulee, remove it (cope).
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If veins or nerves affect limbs or main members as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is decay and blackness, so treat until all decay has eaten through to the bone, then heal in various ways until it becomes healthy again; and if not healthy, reconstruct similarly as before, being aware you do not need to go all the way to heaven: uncover and work until reaching the bottom, remove all decay, then restore its place; and if thusly made healthy, that is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If not, understand that the decay is too extensive to reach, there is no other remedy but from nature's course; and if there are small corrupted bones present, you may extract them with pliers, using a suitable instrument for this purpose, and if many bones exist, remove all of them without exception; and if moisture acts adversely, causing neither error nor fear, protect the site and keep it dry, and liberate the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place something unpleasant and putrefying on the wound, allowing it to be surrounded by bone; then they will more easily have their bones removed; and if it is a large bone, like of leg or thigh, repeatedly cleanse the decay until all the bone is gone, then close the wound; and if there is a significant portion affected by corruption, reaching near to molten bone; it must be entirely covered up to the point of corruption, and then cured until solidified; and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, from which you can take example and assistance for your practice.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 Once upon a time there was a youth not more than thirty years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that came into the body, so much that substances reached the leg and were expelled through a large abscess, with no other reason for it to be opened; however, by their folly doctors worked enough on it until they cut open the abscesses, and consumed a great deal of materials, and it became an fistula. A lot of pus was coming out from all over his body; many doctors treated him for two years, without any healing in the art of hands, until I was called upon, and when I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what was flowing through the fistulas to a large part of his body. His body would turn red as a youth, and had an orange-like color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I built a tent over one of these points, and then searched all the points, finding that each came into contact with the other from every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 Thus I proceeded, and made an incision until I discovered a part of the bone, which was corrupted and felt, reaching corruption up to the inner side of the bone; it appeared as if only that piece of corrupted bone existed apart from others. I began treating the wound with medicinal poultices for a long time but could not heal it; so I started again and found the same in the bone, continuous corruption persisted within the bone which I exposed, and then reattached, and attempted to stitch at that location. But despite cutting around nearly an inch of bone, the entirety tore easily apart once more. I treated it with medicines again; soon after, it became healthy and quickly sealed up without further complications due to only the weakness of the patient who could not endure much pain and fearing death for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 For the evacuation of blood is often soiled, but he was entirely sound, and in the place of the bone arose a hard clot, which was well-formed and had no harm or opposition at all, neither on approach nor on departure.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, do it thus: take a line (ligature), and stretch it at the head of the bone that has been torn apart, and command no one to move it upward; then take another piece of linen larger than the first ligament, tie it over the clot on the bone, and pull on the head so that you remove the corrupted clot from below, revealing the clot at the place where treatment is needed, ensuring the suture does not loosen. Place a wick or piece of wood under the bone to warm up the corrupted clot; treat it until one can see and feel the decay, repeating as necessary.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 If the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in a part or on one side, reveal the entire thing; then remove the tissue above it, and move from one part of the corruption to the other, taking care that your touch is no longer than as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, excise the affected joint, and reach the bone or what contains it on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there's nothing but a coping to be done; and if the corruption is on the tip of hand or foot, that thing is very strong indeed, but nevertheless you must seek out that corrosion, as it opens for you; cleanse it by all means possible without causing pain from nerves or tendons; know that incisors and scrapers for covering these bones are many, depending on the position of the bones and their appearance, size, density, subtlety, largeness, smallness, hardness; therefore you must provide each work with its appropriate instrument; know that your craft will show you the instrument you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the indications from the handling of diseases; so consider the instrument needed according to what is necessary.
dou feu	By fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The head may rot or become hollow due to decay within, or from external causes; and when you have administered the medicinal treatment for this corrosion through the use of remedies, but they prove ineffective, then cover that limb up to where the corrosion originates, so that the patient may escape by its means (or die), or due to a greater harm from the faulty member; and the signs are such that the limb turns black as if it had been scorched with fire, after which the corrosion spreads from one limb to another, affecting the entire body. If you act quickly in covering it up, especially if this is caused by a sting or bite from venomous creatures such as scorpions of the sea, snakes, and similar beings, then when the corrosion reaches the head near the collarbone, cover that area so that there is no delay until it reaches the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 If it comes up to the hand, cap its joint, prevent corrosion from reaching the arm; and if it reaches the arm, cap the elbow; and if it passes the elastoid, that's death, with no remedies except for the quantity of its virtue; and thus do what you must when corrosion comes or spreads: if it reaches the first joint, then cap after the next joint; and if it affects the arm, then cap all of it; and if it moves up to the leg, then cap at the knee joint; and if it's above the knee, there is no other remedy but for the malaise patient to die; the manner of capping or soaking the limb must be such that you bind it above and below, extending slender bands from each fastening, then unfasten the strap between the two straps a span wide, until the bone is exposed; then cap or soak, placing one piece of linen on either side, ensuring the suture does not touch healthy tissue, which could cause further injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 If bleeding occurs while working, promptly cauterize the area or apply restraining powders; then return to your medicine until completed, then bind the wounded limb with an obligatory ligature and treat it until healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man: a blackness appeared that seemed like fire scorching on his thumb joints, consuming the entire fingers. When the man saw the corrosion, he cauterized the hand and was healed; many years later, the corrosion reappeared in his hand from his arm, coming to me, and I treated him with impactful remedies after body purification, but could not stop the corrosions. Doubt arose whether I should cut his hand, as my hope of rebinding the matter remained; so he despaired and returned home, cauterizing his own hand and was healed again. I have no other stories like this to share unless one wishes for alternatives on what can be done if needed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 At no time does an abscess occur in its original place, and it remains so long that it forms a large mass of pus; then they burst and perforate, causing the pus to flow, and the eyelids remain closed like shutters; and the skin above is as fine as cut silk, not reaching even to the bone or nerve, thus such illnesses are called "healthy" and not "fistula"; but if it becomes so extended that it reaches the bone entirely, then it is a fistula. And the skin must be removed completely around it; especially when it is as fine as cut silk.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 And if you have faith that the skin is inflamed, and there is no rot at its core, and the skin has a scent of fresh blood, then apply an enema in this manner: check if the cheeks are large, and the bow which is there smells bad, then prepare the Egyptian medicine thusly: take ease, oil, and litargur equally, and cook it in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and thickens like honey; afterwards add according to your need, mix with water and hebrews, strain into the cheeks, and compress the nostrils. Leave the medicine for two hours then remove by pressing out; repeat this many times until the cheek becomes normal and the pores are clear; do not use an enema of water from ashes unless this Egyptian medicine is present, but if it's not you can take ash from grapevine wood, boil in water and apply with a cloth. After that, if the patient cannot tolerate either the Egyptian medicine or the enema with honey and mild wine, then use an enema of just water and honey with a bit of litargur mixed; otherwise mix with sweet vinegar as honey cleanses and wine strengthens health. Once you have done this, if you are certain that the cheeks have been restored properly, apply an ointment to promote hair growth in that area using aloes wood or malleable iron oil in mead; alternatively use different medications and unguents as I mentioned their properties earlier for ointments. If the nostrils within the enema are too small and cannot receive the liquid, slightly widen them with a piece of iron then apply an Egyptian or basilisk ointment until they have expanded; if the wound is very wide, let it be cauterized as much as needed for the clay to enter.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 When the bow is in fullness, do not leave it uncovered with hair; and if you cannot cover the chest without what you see, prepare it so that the bow falls to the lowest point where it is, for when the bow is in fullness, do not leave it uncovered with hair and if you cannot cover the chest as you see, then arrange: that the bow falls gently downwards, and leaves nothing of the bow; and take medicines strengthening for placing on the saint, and extend over a linen cloth that covers all the saint; then cover the forces spot on the edge of the chest slightly wider than the first, since apply ointment under another cloth according to the quantity of the spot, and put it under the spot on the saint to lighten the bow, and do not remove the large cloth until after many days once; and that which is on the edge of the chest will often be removed to remove the bow, and know where it runs from the bow, whether it's venom or a bit or quite much, or digested, or indigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or numbness, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in such manner and you see the nature underneath the edge of the chest, know that the chest will swell again, and approach healing; then remove it in the morning, or after a day, and when you open the wound, change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 If subtle corruption comes after long time, do not despair of health, for healing is nearing.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.
