de l’aposteme de l’ungle	For the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 A boil is an abscess that arises from under the nail of the hand or foot, or occasionally in other joints; and when it matures, and one does not take care, then many abscesses develop, and burns and pus flow until they reach the root of the nail, and perhaps they devour all; and there come inflammations up to the bone, causing great pain, and the joint is swoln broadly, and the color turns dusky.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you treat it as we have said in the section on treatment, and the remedy does not help, then you must cut all the excess tissue associated with the nail, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The caulteries are very helpful if the bone is healthy, and the nail is clean; and if the nail presses on a vein, and it begins to throb and bruise, then you should place your needle underneath the nail where the blood starts, push upward, and carefully drain the subtle blood before applying remedies that are heating and corrosive to remove everything; then treat with ointments until it is healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 If corrosion is in the bone and you drain it, and treat forcefully because as long as the bone is corrupted there, it cannot heal; and if you see a joint being corrupted, then drain it as previously mentioned, treating until it is healthy. And if it is severe and swollen, causing great pain, first relieve it; then remove the nail with a spatula-like tool cutting across beneath it, but be careful that you do not reach to the vein underneaturessince the patient would feel too much pain; and if so, apply something above that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain in the hand must be soothed
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The dislocation that exists in the shoulders of some people by chance is entirely fleshly, and sometimes there are bones present, and at times a single one; none of them arise from the root of the joint where their origin lies within the shoulders.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 Those that arise in any part of the shoulder do not move, and those that originate at the joint of the shoulder sometimes move; the build of someone fleshly is light, shaping them with a wide span from their root.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born in the joint's root is difficult to treat; use your thumb for this.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In those whose shoulder arises or continues in us, it is necessary to first remove the roundness up to the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, and then heal until it is sound.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come with bone fractures occur through birth, or from the severity of a wound, or scorching heat, or similar causes.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 If it is necessary to treat the swelling, so that they are repaired according to their natural forms; then place between two tents or linen cloths smeared with oil of roses, ensuring they do not stick together; or place between two pieces of fine plank until the joints are fused as needed.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the joining comes to either of its ends with the palm, cover that joinery accordingly as it should be.
des vils	 Of evil spirits
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 These are large wounds swollen with excessive and melancholic humors that come to various body parts; and more often occurs in the legs of those who walk barefoot and work and carry loads, than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore that you should administer an enema once and then purify with salt of the balsamic ointment.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The treatment of iron is in two ways: one is to cut them and drain the black blood; and the other way is that you open the vein and drain it completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The body is treated in this manner: raise the first leg with hot water very strong so that the bone becomes subtleized, then support the leg by the patient's thigh up to the area below the hip; then tie off the vein at one place, either once, twice or three times, with a wide cuff; and extract and pull out the black blood as much as possible from hand to hand until what remains can tolerate its virtue; and then apply bandages, and command that it be dressed in dark meats; and again begin evacuation and healing when the veins are clear, without harming the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The treatments for this condition are as follows: lift the affected leg if it has much hair, then place it in a bath; raise the leg with hot water until it turns red and swells the veins; if you have no bath, heat it over fire and then tie off the vein at the length from head to hip or below the ankle; work on the skin near the bone, and scrape the vein from each side until you can feel it; when it appears red and black, resembling a white cord; push paste underneath until it rises up with the skin, then tie lightly to another place three finger widths above; scrape the skin off the vein as much as possible, then elevate at the joint, just as you have done before, and bind it again to another joint if necessary. Then apply another bandage or more if needed, and wrap around the foot's joint, pulling until reaching the second layer of skin; gradually remove each layer, repeating this process until all is removed, then apply a compress; if unable to extract and lift, use a sharp needle through a strong double thread, insert it into the vein, and turn your hand back and forth until emptied. Be sure not to cut as that would prevent extraction or lifting, causing harm to the patient; after treating completely, place clean linen soaked in wine and oil over the wound site; continue care until healthy again.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the bone is twisted and wrapped together as a whole, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must split it crookedly but not cover it completely; and treat it as we have previously mentioned.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The form of the iron with which you cap the bone is curved, and does not cut, so it covers the vein; and has a large curvature, for if it were fine, it would injure the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, this is the form:
de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein is situated in legs, warm parts where there are no herbs or trees and the ground does not retain moisture; and sometimes it can be found elsewhere than on the legs, occurring from putrefaction that comes from under the skin like what happens inside the body with serpents and worms hiding between skin and muscle.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 When the signs of this vein's beginning occur, a great inflammation comes to the leg, then the lice change, and the vein starts to protrude outward like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 When the head opens up, it must be wrapped with a piece of linen from 2 to 3 inches above and below the wound, leaving the bandage on the leg as much as necessary; every time it becomes loose or comes off, wrap around the liner and wound; if it is too long, cut a part of it, and wrap the remainder without covering its root until it's fully exposed; for if you cover it, it will reopen in the flesh, leading to abscesses, putrefaction, or other diseases. Therefore, it must be treated slowly and gradually until nothing remains inside or outside; on no occasion is this vein left when treated with 5-10 hands wide, or for a man who experienced an opening of 10 hands long, and when you cover it, it causes one to vomit blood or pus, perforating all the way down until emptying itself inside. Then remove the matter within using medicinal poultices every day, then treat as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 Et never to the vein hands rain, and especially when it opens in the joint of the foot or toe, and there is much swelling, and which it bursts out; treat as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 From the veins that arise between flesh and hair.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This illness is called in our land "ox disease," because it often occurs in the bile and is a small worm that arises between skin and hair, moving up and down throughout the body, causing discomfort from one limb to another until it pierces the skin where it goes, bursting out strongly; and it suffers from putrefaction of certain humors as they come in serpents, luminarias, and ascarids or intestines. Doubt arises regarding its nature because when it travels through the body, it ascends to the head, reaches the eye, and on occasion returns, destroying the eye; this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you see it being drawn and emptied, one cannot move unless when emptying occurs: therefore, securely bind the location above and below a strong joint well, then cut near it, and if blood flows out in abundance into the wound, cauterize with fire until it stops; the greatest harm it causes is that oil may come forth as we have said; and if you see it approaching or close to the opening, firmly press down on the eyebrow, then cut near, and draw off the blood; one should use cleaning of the body with medicinal solutions for removing bad humors, and treat with putrefied meats.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 from the pain arising from windwounding
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This illness is called "vacik" in our land, and it causes pain that moves from one limb to another; and this is what I have seen with my own eyes.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was called to see a sickly woman, and I discovered swollen arms, and saw a small inflammation in the vein of her arm; then shortly after, I noticed it ascending like a worm up to the shoulder, faster than any other thing, similar to silver when cut from one place to another; the pain left that location, and moved to the shoulder, and then spread throughout the body until it reached the other arm; she told me that she felt it returning inward around her body, as I had seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 Nevertheless, I wanted to maintain that the pain would move from one place to another, but I did not observe this as in the woman; and I thought it was because she had dry skin, and veins exposed, and hence appeared constrained bloating; and neither do those who are delicious nor those with moist skin and reopened veins exhibit such a reason.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And when you see to treat this disease, and the patient feels that pain if they reveal it as we have said, apply a poultice above and below quickly, and then bandage until the constrained bloating subsides at its place; and cauterize the area; and if you do not see it with your eyes, treat as for those who alleviate flatulence, such as foul pills, serpentine pills, and similar things.
des saiettes	 of arrowheads
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrowheads are of various kinds, according to their appearances and the places in the body where they embed themselves.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 There are various kinds among them, some with large points and small ones, feathered or joined; others have two angles, others with tongues, and those that break into pieces in any part of the body—whether it is a primary member like the brain, heart, liver, stomach, kidneys, intestines, bladder, etc., they all fracture in one of two ways: either within the main members such as mentioned, or elsewhere.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When it breaks in any of these parts of the body, and signs of death appear as I will describe hereafter: one must be wary during the extraction of this arrowhead because death approaches in various ways afterward; but if this sign does not become apparent and the arrowhead is not deeply embedded, then treat and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And the sign of the brain when the arrow enters and pierces the bone is that it jumps and shakes, causing headache, dizziness, vertigo, redness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasm and distortion of understanding, vomiting of bile; and perhaps there is no strength from the nose or ears; and perhaps speech and voice are affected; and a wound with moist white appearing like hairs, similar to being burned by charcoal; and if this sign becomes apparent, pursue the treatment, remove the arrow unless it's already exited.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 The sign of the arrow when it pierces or hits a body part is that it feels near the left breast and seems as if inserted into something hard, not hollow; and sometimes the arrow moves like hairs, and comes out black blood, with coldness coming in, and pale sweat, and fainting: be aware then of doubt leading to death.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of arrow wound is that its normal appearance does not have plain foam coming from the wound; instead, the throat swells, and the patient's complexion changes, they gasp loudly, and ask for cold water.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow pierces into the abdomen near the ribs, then it is close to small intestines; and produces a lot of pus and great pain and gasping; and all limbs shake uncontrollably.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	they le T1 is:t's (b J. Do so: M. The 5-e a, the pique by;llt'm and m, but n’d.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	When the arrow falls into the belly and does not exit through the intestines, there is no hope for its recovery or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder and the urine does not pass through it, causing strong pain to the patient; know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, as it is made and the neck and throat and shoulder and joints and spine of the back and ribs and thighs, and the limbs appearing to be safe, according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not poisonous, as I shall tell you how it happened to me, so that you may do likewise.

And extracted from a body an arrow that was lodged in the fat underneath the paper below it, and the arrowhead was thrust back, only reaching the tip towards its base, being large like those shot from a Turkish bow without any ear protection; the wound healed well, with no adverse occurrences.

And extracted an arrow from the throat of a Christian; it was a Middle Eastern-style arrowhead with ear protection: I removed the barbs, and carefully continued to extract until the Christian was unharmed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And pierced by an arrow at the liver, which was close to the belly, and I thought it would die; but after thirty days had passed, its condition did not change; I cut near the arrow, manipulated it, extracted it successfully, and there were no adverse consequences.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And if an arrow falls onto the back causing a sutured wound; and remains lodged inside, without altering its natural disposition or finding harm in any of its natural functions.

And pierced an arrow in the man of high rank, the king, lodged near his chest and slightly inclined to the right; the arrow was fully embedded after three days when I was called for treatment.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 If I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 He tried with all subtlety, but did not feel it; and he felt neither pressure nor pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 I thought it was from the tip of the arrowhead and placed on the location astringent and digestive to prevent swelling since his eyes were not inflamed, and then the eye sockets became visible due to the arrowhead.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 I placed the astringent overnight and dried out the wound thoroughly, so that the patient rested for long periods until he felt the arrow inside his nose; then he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 I applied a corrosive ointment overnight until it softened and tried to pull the arrowhead out; then I exposed the wound with that same medicine until the head of the arrow became visible; after passing through all its extremities in about four months, I tended to the sores on both sides, but they could not come out. Then I stopped trying directly and devised various methods of extraction until one day I managed to extract it successfully with pliers made according to this book's instructions by following its final recommendations, leaving the wound closed.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the masters judge that the fracture of the nose cannot be restored: I will reset it then, and the wound is securely closed, and the patient becomes entirely healthy.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 Or have I told you the quality of arrow extraction, so that you apply your treatment where I do not mention; for the book cannot cover everything; but wise masters know a great deal, and on what is present and failing, they work with nine works and nine instruments, dealing with strange occurrences in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows are found in limbs where they are deeply embedded either by the front or from another side; and those that burst forth through their entry point, are transverse lodged in fleshly tissues, and cannot break at any time now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai. des voinnes dou cors communes	common bodily illnesses
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 The veins of which we are aware are XXXI in number, including the chief XVI as follows: II Batans located behind the ears, called "herbech"; and II arteries visible in II temples; II veins situated in II temple corners ("aspires"); a vein right at mid-forehead; a vein at the crown of the head where the hairline is; II jugular veins that are present on the neck collarbone area; the II veins that run above the lips, known as "augeherich"; and two veins located beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins which are commonly bled in each arm: one is the cephalic, and is located near the left side, and they call it "vein of the head"; and the other is called "fast", composed of the cephalic and basilic, and they call it "vein of the body"; the basilic is on the right side, and they call it "vein of the belly," and it lies under the bend, and that's the one from which blood is commonly drawn, clearly visible above the armpit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 And the salvatic vein is between the little finger and the ring finger, with two branches; in the leg where the foot is, there are three veins: one under the hollow of the left armpit called "cubitus", another at the ankle on the right side called "sophene"; the one called "nether" which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg, there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The illness of the veins that are after the ears also aids in ancient sweating and migraines; and the condition of the vessel, as I have told you, is to raise the head of the patient, and rub the area where the veins are with an abrasive cloth; then tighten their collar with a cord until the two veins appear behind the ears in two lobes depending on the skull: hold them at your finger joints, and wherever you feel hair above your wrist, clamp it off; then take the lancet, and insert it under the vein to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein towards yourself, and scrape and cut the skin and vein clean with two strokes, allowing blood to flow until you see enough; then tie and ligate it until it is healed; and I have already told of the incision and cautery as in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre. de la sainie des leivres	 From the inflammation of the joints
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The sickness of veins on top leads to dryness in the mouth, and gum decay, and splits in the lips, and bad breath and inflammation.

des sainies de ventouse	 The sentences of blood from bladder pressure relief
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Blood-letting is done with horns, or glass, or crystal; and phlebotomy is performed in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 The ventilation methods of this procedure are as follows: one is done throughout the body with fire; and another with bloodletting. This method involving cutting and extracting blood occurs at 14 different locations on the body: one above the head, one in the neck, two along each side of the neck, under the chin, over both shoulders, over shins (calves), over both arms, over both legs, and over both ankles. The ventilation from these areas does not produce blood but rather small veins scattered throughout the body; therefore, it cannot be performed in every individual as with a vein puncture, so this method should only be administered when no other treatments are effective for diseases caused by excess accumulation until all parts of the body have been emptied.
