Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	If the veins of the legs swell openly, they draw blood from all over the body; they are effective for ancient pains of cold rain, and urination, and bladder problems; and they relieve the throbbing of the two shinbones, and both ankles, and in any case, they weaken the body after long use, bringing pain to various dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the cuff is that you first put it on an empty vein and quickly squeeze it off, then place it hastily, and move evenly, continuing without stopping until you see the redness and swelling of the vein, and blood appears pink; then release, remove the cuffs, and observe the body'cuish position because there are some who have tanned skin and clear pores: if it is necessary to prick only once, make wide and somewhat deep incisions; squeeze gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is large, it should be pricked twice: the first time to make a fine opening for the thick blood flow.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	If the bone is very thin, one must strike a third time; and when we wish to draw out a little blood at a time, we only do so once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if we desire much blood, repeat often; and if the vein is wide, pierce deeply, and terminate so that the vessel be cut swiftly, and it is fitting for those with thick and hard skin, and who are prone to inflammation, to anoint the elbow joints with oil aperitif and dissolutive: if this is so, use violet or almond softening oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is a wound, use cress or lily of the valley, or chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of aniseed, or balm oil, or oil of anise, and similar substances.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 If the one whom you treat has a tender and wide throat, there is no need to apply oil, but after the ventilation with rose water, or cold water, or blackthorn berry water, or gourd plant water, or porcelain water, or any similar substance.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those with much moisture should rise easily, or use myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 Those with large swellings should rise from old wine, or blackthorn berry water, or anet root decoction, or chamomile, or other similar substances; and they must not be bled before the bath nor during it but one hour after the bath, and they must not sleep after ventilation, as they need to sweat when due for bleeding.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And beware of those who are pale and colicky, and whose blood is too hot and inflamed; it is necessary for them to ingest cooling things, such as pomegranates, endives, lettuces with ease, and similar items; mint preserves, chestnut cake, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And those with a cold complexion should ingest syrup of honey, and fragrant wine that is neither old nor new, along with small portions, mint preserves, pignons, little birds, and turtledoves; and for the day they rest, they must drink more than eat. It is necessary to give some individuals triacle or musk before ventosation or afterward to strengthen the main limbs, but be subtle with their blood intake, only those who are too hot should consume it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 The suction cups that are placed without causing harm are those put on the liver and kidneys, and gout, and on the belly, bowels, groin, and ankle, for these limbs do not suffer to be touched anywhere, but only done so in order to draw blood from one part of the body to another, as we place them on the nipples when they are healing; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we place suction cups on the belly and anus to reduce the limb; and relieves pain when there is obstruction or stone, so it may draw out the blockage by chance, or leave the stone from its original location; and thus works when placed on the liver and kidnecups when viscosity is retained, and these suction cups are arranged to empty as much as possible; and sometimes they are filled with steam, and sometimes with plain water, such as in illnesses of pleurisy, and in this way one fills the suction cup with hot water alone, or water that has boiled herbs suitable for it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of filling the blister with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it should have two fingers wide and a half palm at the base, and around the vein insert a small needle hole as if to push in a needle, and use thread made of silk, so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and around there should be a cross-threaded wire or iron, for placing a candlewick, and they should vary in size large and small depending on the diseases and nature of those who take them; because children's cupping sets are different from old ones, and lighter than fatter.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And this is how you should apply the cupping glass to the limb: take a waxed candle or tallow and insert it through the cross-threaded wire which is within the cupping set, so that its glow does not burn the patient at the bottom of the cup; then place the glass on the limb, and ensure that underneard there is the small hole we have mentioned, so that when desired, steam will come off, and you can remove the cupping set; then take the tallow as before, and begin again frequently, if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the cupping which is applied for pleurisy disease, in freshness, it has no penis or scrotum, and it is made only when filled with water, and is placed on the limb fully. And this is how it looks like:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Without cupping, they are applied only to limbs where you cannot place cups due to smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; also in nude flesh like the genitals, and others; and their quality is that when you find cups filled with pure soft water, take them; put one at a time into soft water until they become accustomed, without anything in their bellies; then let it bleed and apply cupping again, rub the limb until it turns red, and place the cups; and once they are full and adhere, if you can place a cup there, do so, because it is greatly beneficial.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If not, raise the joint with ease, then apply much water, and afterwards press; and if the vessel is still swollen after removing from the body without a sinew, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and place it on top until the bone is compressed; and if there are multiple fractures, use powdered vitriole or gales, among other things, until they are compressed; now put two-thirds of peeled leeks on it, leaving them until they harden to the joint, which will compress it now; and if you need more liniments, take others.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 If the bones do not begin to knit, rub the joint with fresh blood or insert a needle until it pierces through, and then place them on top; as soon as they feel the blood, they will harden; when you see that they are oozing, powder some aloe and sage broth, or ash, upon them, which will cause them to become solid.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This book of fractures begins
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are often necessary in the art of medicine, and they involve the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Learn from this treatise, oh wise man, that the foolish may be enlightened by its teachings, which you will never find in any of the ancient books or letters read; and for this reason, knowledge is strange on our land, as I have found no good examples; although I know nothing unless through the wisdom of ancient texts, with which I have studied so much that I have mastered their knowledge, and by experimentation, and from the habits of my life; and herein I describe to you what is contained within this chapter, summarizing it at its end, and clearly showing the forms of remedies applied as shown in these two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we should say or preface of this book the essence of its words and chapters in which the wise place their understanding, staying close to truth so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 I say that when there is a fracture or dislocation or torsion or swelling in any part of the body, it is necessary to bind the patient on both sides if nothing covers them entirely, as with frailty of limbs or infants or elderly; and if the time is not too warm or too cold; and consume chilled broths such as poultry and veal stock, do not drink wine or any fatty soups, and do not fill yourself up excessively with meats that cause blood vessels to be filled, until you no longer have doubt of an abscess or discharge of matter from the limb; then it is time for the patient to rest as they are accustomed.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, one should nourish the patient with foods that promote growth, such as those causing viscosity (as cooked wheat in water), beets, eggs, liver, veal stomach, and offal, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar items.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	In certain cases of dislocation, movement is restored quickly but then fractures occur soon afterward.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that old and decrepit bones cannot be well mended or welded according to their nature for the strengthening of limbs, nor those as in young children's; but do not care, reset on the broken bone with large tongs which are strong and join the member together until it becomes firm like before; and there is nothing left from your work, and therefore you must nourish them with fat meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	to (a:
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	The fractures of the head are different from those of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	There are fractures that resemble an arch, and others like sharpening wood, similar to the tip of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with an open wound, and a fracture that's just a tiny split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And each way has its own device and instrument for restoration, according to what comes to mind at the time; and it is known that a bone is broken by how much the joint is twisted, clearly bent out of place, and under pressure from hand manipulation; but if there is no twisting or catching, and the patient does not feel great pain unless there is a fracture. But he may well have twisting, or splitting, or small fractures.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	; d the so plee ond;
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that the fracture which is in suspense, and are the two parts disjointed, they must now be set evenly, just as if an abscess were to come; and if an abscess arises, leave it for no day until it is soothed; then set it even to movements you can move easily and gently, and know that its restoration is easier than the one where there are pieces; then strain, as it should be hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And if the bone is broken into pieces, divided into two parts, whether it's hands or feet, or a small member, or to your hand, if it's one cord, or a single cord and your hand; then place the limb according to its natural figure so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, you reset them by all means back into their places with movements you can do, and ensure through your work there is no injury or pain to the patient; and align well the two ends of the bone in accordance with the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And if the patient's hand feels not quite right to you: clean it well, and do not strain or press it too much as those who bring forth abscesses and constrictions through their work often have done, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the limb is at a standstill, chastise the patient well so they do not move, neither in wakefulness nor sleeping, nor turning, or any other way; and ensure that the limb is secure enough that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 For when it feels no pain, it is not at a standstill, and you must put it in such a position that it feels no pain; and ensure that it is placed straightly, so as to avoid any twists if restored; the quality of the injured limb depends on what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	That broken limbs vary in size and extent and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 For small members such as arms and legs: you must wrap them with soft fine linen; for larger ones like hips and thighs: use a wide sturdy bandage, as the wider bandages encompass the entire limb evenly so there are no imbalances; then place light padding around it three or four turns depending on the member, then hold one end of the bandage tight for the whole length, then move to above the break and loosen slightly, with the break moving slightly away from the body; then gradually soften the bandages little by little until you grasp a large part of the healthy portion, then use another bandage and return directly over the broken area; then go back to the area below the break, and tighten moderately, not too hard or too loosely as we have said in the first instruction above; then place linen strips between the bandages so they are all even, then wrap everything with a belt upwards until it is covered completely, unless there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 If there is swelling or an abscess, apply a soothing ointment to the abscess and remove the swelling, leaving it as such for several days; then bind with bandages of moistened broad leather strips, or wood made into splints, or palm fronds, according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 However, it is necessary that the splint placed on the fracture be slightly larger and wider than the others; and as long as required for limbs of small or large size; then bind with bandages as you did in the initial setting, then tie above a thread promptly, similarly to the first setting over the fracture; tighter is less. It must be that the thread be moderate, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, like I have seen in works where people make their rope knots from flax cords, it is a great error, as the splint cannot be evenly spaced if they are too fine.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is in pain from the heads of the nails after pulling them out in their healthy places, then apply cotton or cloth scraps between them so they do not pierce through.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the bone is broken, I will describe the treatment as follows.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And remember that it does not require extracting all splinters from the fractured limb on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 When the limb is large, it must not be set with splints too soon after V or VII days, or more depending on the risk of a sudden abscess; and here is the ancient way to restore breaks, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that stands as if by the walls of a mill, mix it with much egg white, and make this mixture, not too clear nor too thick, for use. This is the common method of the splint restoring broken bones in various positions, especially among women and small children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of ointment for healing fractures and dislocations and twists: take resin, laudanum, elecampane root, asafoetida, gum arabic, etc., about 12 parts; myrrh and aloes, about 5 parts; benzoin .viiij. parts; and in a powder form, honeycomb with beef fat; if the patient's constitution is hot, use this ointment as it has good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, benefiting many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another splint method for torsion: take mugwort and cumin, in quantities of 10 by the horn; myrrh and aloes, in amounts of 9 by the horn; achillea, in volumes of 6 by the horn; bolus Armeniac, in volumes of 10 by the horn, and finely grind it. Then mix with water or abundant egg white to prepare.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another method of resetting dislocated joints and exposed bones is to find new ones; relieve the pain occurring, cut away the bone, and fracture: take fresh thread, and boil the wool in oil, and place it on the location.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 These dressings do not heal but are good for cooling abscesses and properly alleviating pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to set broken bones: take dry leaves of fig trees and ground ivy leaves, grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another method of dressing is to promote the healing of bone fractures and cool any remaining abscesses.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take root of valerian, chamomile, violet flowers, flour from honey; and grind it up, then mix with wine. If the limb is swollen, dilute with wet coriander water or plain water, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another method of treatment more effective than the first, when an abscess comes to heal the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take the roots of wormwood, and flaxseed, balm, mallow, mustard seeds, and flowers from violets and chamomile, in equal parts; grind them together, then boil with salt water or freshwater, or wine according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras states in his book that one should not apply anything on a broken limb for healing other than wax and oil mixture, and it should be of neither too hard nor too soft consistency.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And according to Galen, on must apply dry and slightly warm substances such as myrrh, aloe, incense, and similar things for healing a broken limb, as we have said before.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plastering for injuries and pain: take crushed mullein and chamomile flowers or feathers of birds, and wormwood, all in equal quantities, grind them together, and make the plaster with honey.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then loosen slightly after a while and be sure the patient feels no pain or has shifted any bones in their joints; do not loosen too quickly. If pain comes to the joint, or itching, with rest or swelling, act swifttly and loosen again, apply the poultice now; take light linen, a wet sponge, dip into water, lift up the limb until the itch ceases and the pain subsides; then let the limb rest for an hour, then wrap in dry cloth wetted with water or oil rosset, tied under a nut until you are sure of high heat; and soothe inflammation of the joint and remove the pain, then resume gentle exercise, and apply some poultice again, but not as strongly as before; continue gently until fully healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess and redness and pain and swelling are throughout the bone, and you need plaster and bandages, when you resume as you did before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 If it comes to the limb with nothing of what we have said, do not reset until after III days or IV or V or VII; and never leave it unset for XX days, as seen by the time when the breaker heals, and approaches the joint above; then you should hold it tighter than initially, and let the flesh swell, as I have mentioned before; and if you see that drying occurs more than necessary, know that no complications will arise; hence provide hot water frequently whenever you reset it, and do so every day, and moisten slightly often. This way, complications in the limb are avoided, and emulate promptly what skilled physicians do, who return the joint properly: this is harmful, and these procedures are fearsome, and I see nothing else but fatigue and proper work.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 Many ways of breaks are, and various forms, and the causes are distinguished; for there are breaks made by sword blows, where the bone is split through to the joint below the bone, as if made with an axe or cudgel; and therefore this type of break is called "axiless".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	it is not s and sentence of the f for:
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	If there is an impacted object, or crack or stone shards, or falling on stones, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a hernia that reaches the skin close to the bone, or above it, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if there is a wound that has been sealed to the bone as delicate as mouse hairs, and it is a small fracture, therefore this type of break is called "capillary"; and if the wound is made by being hit with a stone or falling, or other similar things, where part of the bone enters inside, and lies above like bellows when they are fired on the hearths; among them within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 This occurs more often in those who have wet bones like children's skulls, and it happens in all these ways of fractures where small pieces are not properly dealt with as such; and I will speak to them specifically.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all ways of fractures from the pull above them, and investigation with attempts, and by the corrupted cartilage which is below.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known because when an bone is discovered and rubbed over with heat, it shows the black break.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a break, beware of any malaise by accident, and if you see no ill-fated accidents such as vomiting black bile, loss of mind, extension, paleness, fever ague, eyes protruding and turning red, and other similar dispositions, do not heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you do not see an easily hopeful injury, and if you expect healing, then begin treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the swelling comes to you first, and it is in winter, then remove the bone after the fourteenth day on which you can move.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day so that the flesh underneath the bone becomes corrupted and come the accidents we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 And if the fracture of the bone comes just below the skin that covers the brain, it is necessary to split the broken part thusly; and ensure that you expose as much skull as possible affected by the injury, revealing the bone in all ways you can, and on the wound's surface more than you can, with bleeding occurring when exposing the bone or abscesses appear. You should proceed according to what is necessary; then fill the cavity with moistened bandages soaked in oil of roses; let the wound rest until any pustules are calmed and you're certain about bleeding stopping; then begin around the bone, removing it as follows: one method involves cutting at a narrow opening in front, which is where the form lies.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision wider than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	The second method involves having various types of pincers, some narrow and others wide, with points and made of iron wire; in light work, do not strike the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	If the bone is hard and tough, it is necessary that you drill around it, making indentations with tongs without piercing beyond the skull of the head, ensuring a margin or circle at the tip so that the point does not pass through the bone; and you must have several, so each comes in its place according to the thickness of the bone, having tongs for all tests (types); these are the three ways of making tongs:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for drilling around the bone is to place a tong on the bone and turn it back and forth until you know that the bone has been pierced; then move the tong slightly and do so all around, making a cut with the incisors between the punctures, doing this more delicately than possible, lightly, as we have said, until you come across the bone to your hand or any of the instruments that you have like pincers.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 And when you have pierced the bone and cut, it is necessary to remove any protruding piece of the bone that resembles an instrument similar to a chisel; but it must be more securely fastened and finer than other instruments like it; and if there are no small bones or scale-like fragments remaining, gently use with ointments and bandages as we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is what the Galenians call it, which is more effective; and this one is very strong, and that's my word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover part of the bone where the fracture opens up, and once you have uncovered that part, place it under the top of this lens-shaped instrument; which has the following shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 And do not cut away from the sides, and it is an inflamed part in two ribs, so that the cutting tool faces the bone; then strike gently with a small mallet underneath, so that you chip the entire bone lightly without harming the covering tissue above it; if it's loose to the bone, loosen the bone slightly, as doing otherwise may cause damage and fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone fracture does not pierce through to the skin and is cut slightly above, with small pieces remaining, you must treat that severity again, and remove scales using a subtle razor of which you should have various quantities in order to apply most conveniently at each location according to the work and shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If using many large razors first, then more subtle ones, continue doing so until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair cuts and subtle breaks, you must treat according to their directionality; and this is something not easily repaired by those who have devoted themselves to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 If the face is uncovered, it is necessary that you pick a linen bandage according to the quantity of the wound, and grease with oil rose, and place it over the wound; then take another padded bandage folded in two or three layers, and grease with wine and oiled rose, and place it above the first bandage; and do this gently so as not to burden the face, afterwards apply from below other remedies, and do not stretch it more than necessary for the wound alone; leave it like that for one or two days until the abscess swelling is calmed down, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, ground flaxseed, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; from these things make a fine powder, place it on the ward, and administer additional medicines without irritation; and ensure that the wound remains clean, so you do not leave any grease or debris inside.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore be cautious, if anything unexpected comes to the patient as we have mentioned, it is questionable without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if blackness comes not from the medicine applied there, but to ensure its virtue, you must take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil mixed with woolen cloth, then apply it on the swelling; then care for it as needed until it becomes healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Sections that are never broken above or below the neck, for they are two bones; and one is cartilaginous and does not break but twists or folds, then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And if one of the two parts is broken, you must tie a small bandage or cloth near the neck, and place the break inside your index finger's sheath, then up to the throat on the other side, until the vein returns to its natural shape; do this gently, ensuring the patient feels no pain from your procedure.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the neck and cannot bring the thumb to its place, it should be set as level with a small piece of wood.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 And if the break is in two parts, do likewise again, and hasten to repair it within one day if you can; if not, after seven or eight days when the swelling has subsided, then bandage near the neck with linen strips of cloth, if the break is on one side.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you bind another from the other side, if there is a fracture therein; and let the sutures be so large that they fill the pores with blood.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And some surgeons say one must pull out the threads with butter, and change them daily.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 It seems to me that this may not be the best course of action, but it should be done with a mixture of egg white and powdered miller's flour, then leave the thread alone until the bone is fully healed and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And at no time should one put goose feathers on the suture site, and if there is a cloth bandage around it, and hold the breakage, and blow away the bad spirits; as you see fit do so.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess occurs in the nose while you work on it, then apply a poultice or cotton ball soaked in rose oil or a bit of diaconicon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if an abscess does not form, apply the paste afterward, consisting of wheat flour and incense powder mixed with egg white, then place it on light gauze bandages without using pitch; and if a fracture to the nose is small and broken into tiny pieces, extract the fragments as appropriate for this case, then make an incision, and heal other complicated wounds such as char and soldering, like plasters and ointments suitable for that, and if there are no internal injuries of the nostrils, cure with threads, and apply linen strips until it is healthy.

de la forcele	The strengthening of muscles
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fractures break several times before the shoulder, and the breaks are in three ways: one is broken and separated into two parts, and there are fragments, and it is easier to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	Et the work is such when there is a fracture without a wound, so you need two assistants, one who treats the dislocated shoulder that feels weakness; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then place the fracture to your arms equally, so that it forms as it should, with no appearance or lopsidedness.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place under the patient's shoulder a round rod of cloth or wool, and it should be thick according to your necessity; stretch and ease the dislocation, hold the rod in their hand, so that they align the fracture equally as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the dislocation forward because it comes out on both sides, then let the patient lie down on their stomach, and place under the shoulder a middle-sized pillow; then the assistants lift the shoulder upwards until the bone is elevated.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the break of your arm, and if you find any fragments, it is necessary to split them; and pull out the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join by any means, use a tool from one of the incisions that you have made; but place it under the fulcrum, for this instrument will prevent slippage.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 And it appears as a spoon, and is not straight but wide as needed according to the size of the bone and strength of the work; and have two angles, as you see, one wider and the other narrower, as dictated by the wound from when you set the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, cut the wound, and if the contour is small or there is doubt about it being a hot abscess, cover the wound with cloths and bandages according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	When an abscess occurs there, if it fills with pus, then apply a cloth soaked in oil rose-colored and medicinal wine, and place upon it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 The tightening of the bone when it is without wounds and without movement, you should put on the bone plaster with powdered wheat meal and fat from eggs, then place light bandages over it, and use a large sponge underneath if needed; then take a very large bandage one palm wide, and place double gauze over the bandages and plaster; then take a fine strip three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the head of the bandage hangs down; and place the strip over the fracture, turning the bandage upwards from the collarbone to below it, and from the healthy shoulder to the injured one; tie each part together, and when you see that the ligatures hold the fracture firmly enough, change them every day until they are loosebut, if not used correctly. Let the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow underneath the collarbone to lift the injured shoulder; this will relieve the pressure from the strain by adjusting the position of the shoulder, or you can tie the arm to the neck as long as no bad accidents occur until twenty days; then restart the plaster if needed and keep it on like that until fully healed; usually restored in twenty-eight days, but some less.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of a broken shoulder blade
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 Often it happens that the shoulder breaks or is dislocated and should not be moved except by touch; then arrange according to the nature of the breakage, and reset in its natural form in all ways possible; then put on a powder made from finely ground flour with plenty of water, along with light bandages, then cover with two layers; then place a wide and subtle board slightly wider than the shoulder, ensuring the joint does not move anywhere on the shoulder, so tighten it with linen thread evenly; and then strain firmly for a long time until the board does not move from its spot, observing the ligaments every day; each time if there is loosening, reinforce, and adjust the board if necessary to maintain position, while patients rest on their side; thus the shoulder can be restored in 20 days or 25 days. When these numbers are completed, release it, but be careful, as it's not bone that moves lightly again.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut. de la brisure dou pis	From breaking of the shin bone
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 The fish is sometimes broken on the spit, but it happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the end.

And the healing is that the patient lies on his back, and a pillow is placed between the shoulders, then press down on the shoulders, and binds the ribcage with both hands, doing so in all possible ways until it is rightly aligned; then place casts and padding over the broken bone gently, either with salt or another light substance, and wrap it in a piece of cloth so that it stays still; then return to the normal position on his back, and loosen gradually as needed, and let out each suture after an hour'amo, and if it becomes loose, re-tighten it; and if it needs to be undone for corrosion or pruritus at the site, pain, or abscess, do so quickly, remove what is there, and apply suitable treatment methods; then unwrap the casts, and tighten them as needed until healthy.

de la brisure dou col	of the broken rib
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	There is no time for fractures of the bone in the neck and it does not occur that it bends; also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And when it happens to anyone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, observe carefully if their hands become softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move or extend them, and when you prick the fingers with a needle, if they feel nothing.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure. de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	For breaking of the thighbone

And the restoration is such that you extend your hand over it as long as it's over the break; and identify what kind of fracture and its shape; and if the fracture is only on top, then balance this break to make it naturally shaped.

de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of a fracture of the shoulder

de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	For a fracture of the bone in the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, if she can sit upright, then lean her back towards the painful area and be supported from behind; next fill the balm with cotton as large as it fits; then have the woman stand up slowly bit by bit, and once the cotton slides in to the entrance of the nature, returns with the cotton; and when she needs to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has finished, let it return, and so do this for seven days or more: if done correctly, the fracture will be restored. If you wish, take a hare's bladerocket, tie some woolen cloth at its neck, then fill the entire bladder into the nature; then blow air through the hole in the rocket until the bladder is empty: the nature will return to normal. Then fill it with cotton and leave it like this for several days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. de la forcelle	Of forcefulness
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The strength cannot dislocate the ribs within and below, nor is it ever dislocated without feeling.

de la dislocation de l’espaule	Regarding the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 The shoulder can dislocate in three ways: one is that it dislocates towards the shin area; and the second is to the calf part; sometimes it dislocates upwards, but this occurs rarely; nor does it ever dislocate backwards or inside for nerves; occasionally it dislocates downwards towards the ankle, especially in those with little flesh as they do so quickly; in those with enough flesh, it dislocates slightly and returns easily.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to certain men from a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated by this.
